(O, K, * TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">تُضِيفُ إِلَى صَوْتِ الفَحْلِ</foreign>, said of a she-camel, means <hi rend="ital">She hears with desire of going to him the voice,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sound, of the stallion.</hi> (M.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">الإِضَافَةُ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n26207-1" target="التَّضَايُفُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> signify <hi rend="ital">Correlation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reciprocal relation, so that one of the two cannot be conceived in the mind without the other;</hi> as in the case of <foreign lang="ar">الأُبُوَّةُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">البُنُوَّةُ</foreign> [i. e. fathership and sonship]. (KT. [See also 3.])       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">اضافهُ إِلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He made it to incline towards it;</hi> (S, M, * O, Msb, K; *) namely, a thing (S, O) to a thing. (S, O, Msb.) <hi rend="ital">He made it to lean, rest,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stay itself, against it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">upon it.</hi> (M, TA.)                   <hi rend="ital">He leaned his back against the wall.</hi> (MA.) And <foreign lang="ar">اضاف إِلَيْهِ أَمْرًا</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He rested,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stayed, upon him an affair, and desired him to do what would suffice.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">He made him to have recourse to it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to betake himself to it for refuge.</hi> (S, O, K.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And <hi rend="ital">He adjoined it to it.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And hence <foreign lang="ar">الإِضَافَةُ</foreign> as a conventional term of the grammarians; because the first [of two nouns in the case to which it applies] is adjoined to the second: (Msb:) [for] <foreign lang="ar">إِضَافَةُ الاِسْمِ إِلَى الاِسْمِ</foreign> is [<hi rend="ital">The prefixing the noun to the noun so that the former governs the latter in the gen. case</hi>] as when you say <foreign lang="ar">غُلَامُ زَيْدٍ</foreign>; in which instance, <foreign lang="ar">غلام</foreign> is termed   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n26207-2" target="مُضَافٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n26214"/></foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">زيد</foreign> is termed <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n26207-3" target="مُضَافٌ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n26214"/>إِلَيْهِ</foreign>: and this is done for the purpose of particularizing or appropriating, and of making known or definite: therefore the <foreign lang="ar">إِضَافَة</foreign> of a thing to itself [i. e. the prefixing a noun in this manner to one identical therewith in meaning] is not allowable, because a thing does not make known, or definite, itself; (S;) unless by an ellipsis, as when you say <foreign lang="ar">حَقُّ اليَقِينِ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">حَقُّ الشَّىْءِ اليَقِينِ</foreign>; or, accord. to Fr, the Arabs used to do so because of the difference of the two words themselves. (S voce <foreign lang="ar">جَامِعٌ</foreign>.) [<foreign lang="ar">الإِضَافَةُ</foreign> is also often used as meaning <hi rend="ital">The state of being prefixed in the manner explained above;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the connection of a noun so prefixed with its complement.</hi> The various kinds of <foreign lang="ar">إِضَافَة</foreign> are sufficiently explained in the grammars of De Sacy and others: they are not proper subjects of a lexicon, though much is said respecting them in the O, and more in the Msb.          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  Hence also, <foreign lang="ar">بِالإِضَافَةِ إِلَى كَذَا</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">In comparison with</hi> (lit. <hi rend="ital">to</hi>), or <hi rend="ital">in relation to,</hi> (like <foreign lang="ar">بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">such a thing;</hi> as though <hi rend="ital">in juxtaposition to it:</hi> a phrase of frequent occurrence: see an ex. in Bd ii. 6.]          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَضَفْتُهُ</foreign> (inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">إِضَافَةٌ</foreign>, Msb) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n26207-4" target="ضَيَّفْتُهُ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> (inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَضْيِيفٌ</foreign>, O) both signify the same, (S, M, O, Msb, K,) from <foreign lang="ar">الضِّيَافَةُ</foreign>; (O;) i. e. both signify <hi rend="ital">I made him a guest,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lodged him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">gave him refuge</hi> or <hi rend="ital">asylum,</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَنْزَلْتُهُ</foreign>, (S, M, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">with me, as a</hi>
